matchingMockDev.SignResponse(&u2f.AuthenticateChallenge{\n\t\t\tChallenge: challenge.Challenge,\n\t\t\tKeyHandle: challenge.KeyHandle,\n\t\t\tAppID:     challenge.AppID,\n\t\t})\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t\t// Verify the signature on the server side\n\t\t// BUG: If multiple devices send responses, the server might not correctly\n\t\t// identify which device was used\n\t\terr = as.AuthServer.CheckU2FSignResponse(ctx, user.GetName(), &u2f.AuthenticateChallengeResponse{\n\t\t\tKeyHandle:     signResp.KeyHandle,\n\t\t\tClientData: \"+\n\t\t\t\t\"This could indicate a bug in multi-device challenge verification where \"+\n\t\t\t\t\"the server fails to match the response to the correct device.\",\n\t\t\t\tchallenge.KeyHandle)\n\t\t}\n\t\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"Authentication with registered device should succeed\")\n\t}\n}\n\n// testMultiDeviceChallengeSeparation verifies that challenges are properly isolated\n// between different devices and don't interfere with each other during verification.\nfunc testMultiDeviceChallengeSeparation(t *testing.T) {\n\tctx := context.Background()\n\tclock := clockwork.NewFakeClock()\n\tas, err := auth.NewTestAuthServer(auth.TestAuthServerConfig{\n\t\tDir:   t.TempDir(),\n\t\tClock: clock,\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, mocku2f.Create()\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\tdevice2, err := mocku2f.Create()\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Register device 1\n\tregChallenge1, err := as.AuthServer.CreateRegisterChallenge(ctx, user.GetName(), proto.MFARegisterChallengeRequest_U2F)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\tregResp1, err := device1.RegisterResponse(&u2f.RegisterChallenge{\n\t\tChallenge: regChallenge1.GetU2F().Challenge,\n\t\tAppID:     regChallenge1.GetU2F().AppID,\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\t_, err = as.AuthServer.AddMFADeviceSync(ctx, user.GetName(), \"device-1\", &proto.MFARegisterResponse{\n\t\tResponse: &proto.MFARegisterResponse_U2F{U2F: &proto.U2FRegisterResponse{\n\t\t\tRegistrationData: regResp1.RegistrationData,\n\t\t\tClientData:       regResp1.ClientData,\n\t\t}},\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Register device 2\n\tregChallenge2, err := as.AuthServer.CreateRegisterChallenge(ctx, user.GetName(), proto.MFARegisterChallengeRequest_U2F)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\tregResp2, err := device2.RegisterResponse(&u2f.RegisterChallenge{\n\t\tChallenge: regChallenge2.GetU2F().Challenge,\n\t\tAppID:     regChallenge2.GetU2F().AppID,\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\t_, err = as.AuthServer.AddMFADeviceSync(ctx, user.GetName(), \"device-2\", &proto.MFARegisterResponse{\n\t\tResponse: &proto.MFARegisterResponse_U2F{U2F: &proto.U2FRegisterResponse{\n\t\t\tRegistrationData: regResp2.RegistrationData,\n\t\t\tClientData:       regResp2.ClientData,\n\t\t}},\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Get first authentication challenge\n\tu2fStorage, err := u2f.InMemoryAuthenticationStorage(as.AuthServer.Services)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\tauthChallenge1, err := as.AuthServer.mfaAuthChallenge(ctx, user.GetName(), u2fStorage)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\trequire.Equal(t, 2, len(authChallenge1.U2F), \"Should have 2 challenges\")\n\n\t// Extract challenges for each device\n\tvar chal1, chal2 *proto.U2FChallenge\n\tkh1 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(device1.KeyHandle)\n\tkh2 := base64.URLEncoding.WithPadding(base64.NoPadding).EncodeToString(device2.KeyHandle)\n\n\tfor _, chal := range authChallenge1.U2F {\n\t\tif chal.KeyHandle == kh1 {\n\t\t\tchal1 = chal\n\t\t} else if chal.KeyHandle == kh2 {\n\t\t\tchal2 = chal\n\t\t}\n\t}\n\trequire.NotNil(t, chal1, \"Should find challenge for device 1\")\n\trequire.NotNil(t, chal2, \"Should find challenge for device 2\")\n\n\t// Verify challenges are different (they should be, generated independently)\n\tif chal1.Challenge == chal2.Challenge {\n\t\t// This is actually acceptable - challenges can theoretically be the same\n\t\t// but key handles must be different\n\t\tt.Logf(\"Note: Challenges happen to be the same (OK)\")\n\t}\n\trequire.NotEqual(t, chal1.KeyHandle, chal2.KeyHandle,\n\t\t\"Key handles for different devices must be unique\")\n\n\t// Verify that device 1 cannot authenticate with device 2's challenge\n\t// This is a critical security test\n\twrongSignResp, err := device1.SignResponse(&u2f.AuthenticateChallenge{\n\t\tChallenge: chal2.Challenge,\n\t\tKeyHandle: chal2.KeyHandle,\n\t\tAppID:     chal2.AppID,\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\t// Attempting to authenticate device 1 with device 2's challenge should fail\n\terr = as.AuthServer.CheckU2FSignResponse(ctx, user.GetName(), &u2f.AuthenticateChallengeResponse{\n\t\tKeyHandle:     wrongSignResp.KeyHandle,\n\t\tClientData:    wrongSignResp.ClientData,\n\t\tSignatureData: wrongSignResp.SignatureData,\n\t})\n\tif err == nil {\n\t\tt.Error(\"REGRESSION BUG: Device 1 was able to authenticate with device 2's challenge. \" +\n\t\t\t\"This indicates a critical security issue in multi-device U2F authentication where \" +\n\t\t\t\"challenges are not properly isolated between devices.\")\n\t}\n\trequire.Error(t, err, \"Using wrong device for challenge should fail\")\n\n\t// Now verify that each device CAN authenticate with its own challenge\n\tcorrectSignResp1, err := device1.SignResponse(&u2f.AuthenticateChallenge{\n\t\tChallenge: chal1.Challenge,\n\t\tKeyHandle: chal1.KeyHandle,\n\t\tAppID:     chal1.AppID,\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\terr = as.AuthServer.CheckU2FSignResponse(ctx, user.GetName(), &u2f.AuthenticateChallengeResponse{\n\t\tKeyHandle:     correctSignResp1.KeyHandle,\n\t\tClientData:    correctSignResp1.ClientData,\n\t\tSignatureData: correctSignResp1.SignatureData,\n\t})\n\trequire.NoError(t, err, \"Device 1 should authenticate with its own challenge\")\n\n\t// Create a fresh user.GetName(), u2fStorage)\n\trequire.NoError(t, err)\n\n\trequire.Equal(t, len(deviceNames), len(authChallenge.U2F),\n\t\t\"Expected all registered U2F devices to have challenges\")\n\n\t// Test Only the first registered device receives a challenge, preventing access via other tokens.\n\n### Root Cause\n\nThe bug is located in `/app/lib/auth/auth.go` in the `U2FSignRequest()` method (line 828). The method includes this TODO comment and problematic code:\n\n```go\n// TODO(awly): mfa: support challenge with multiple devices.\ndevs, err := a.GetMFADevices(ctx, user)\nif err != nil {\n    return nil, trace.Wrap(err)\n}\nfor _, dev := range devs {\n    if dev.GetU2F() == nil {\n        continue\n    }\n    return u2f.AuthenticateInit(ctx, u2f.AuthenticateInitParams{\n        Dev:        dev,\n        AppConfig:  *u2fConfig,\n        StorageKey: user,\n        Storage:    a.Identity,\n    })  // <-- EARLY RETURN: only processes first device!\n}\n```\n\nThe method loops through registered devices but returns immediately after the first U2F device, preventing challenges from being generated for subsequent devices.\n\n### Modern Challenge Generation\n\nThe newer `mfaAuthChallenge()` method (line 1920) attempts to fix this by appending all U2F challenges to a slice:\n\n```go\nfor _, dev := range devs {\n    // ...\n    ch, err := u2f.AuthenticateInit(ctx, u2f.AuthenticateInitParams{\n        AppConfig:  *u2fPref,\n        Dev:        dev,\n        Storage:    u2fStorage,\n        StorageKey: user,\n    })\n    if err != nil {\n        return nil, trace.Wrap(err)\n    }\n    challenge.U2F = append(challenge.U2F, &proto.U2FChallenge{\n        KeyHandle: ch.KeyHandle,\n        Challenge: ch.Challenge,\n        AppID:     ch.AppID,\n    })\n}\n```\n\nHowever, this method is private and not used in all authentication flows.\n\n## Test Structure\n\n### Test 1: `testMultiDeviceU2FChallenge`\n**Purpose**: Verify that multiple U2F devices can be registered and challenges are generated for all of them.\n\n**Flow**:\n1. Creates a test auth server with U2F enabled\n2. Creates a user and registers a TOTP device (required for adding other MFA devices)\n3. Registers 3 U2F devices\n4. Verifies all devices are present in the device list\n\n**Expected Failure Indicator**: If the multi-device bug is present, challenges wouldn't be properly presented to the client, though this test primarily validates the registration flow.\n\n### Test 2: `testMultiDeviceU2FAuthentication`\n**Purpose**: Document the expected behavior for multi-device authentication.\n\n**Flow**:\n1. Creates a test user with 2 U2F devices registered\n2. Verifies both devices exist in the device list\n3. Documents the expected authentication flow\n\n**This test establishes baseline expectations for the authentication process**.\n\n### Test 3: `testMultiDeviceChallengeSeparation`\n**Purpose**: Verify that devices have unique key handles and cannot be cross-authenticated.\n\n**Flow**:\n1. Registers 2 U2F devices\n2. Verifies each device has a unique KeyHandle\n3. Tests that a device cannot authenticate with another device's challenge\n4. Tests that each device can authenticate with its own challenge\n\n**Expected Behavior**:\n- ✓ Each device has a unique KeyHandle\n- ✓ Device cannot authenticate with wrong device's challenge\n- ✓ Device authenticates successfully with its own challenge\n\n**Failure Indicator**: If challenge isolation fails, it would indicate a fundamental issue in the multi-device handling.\n\n## How to Run the Test\n\n### Basic Run\n```bash\ngo test -run TestRegression -v -timeout 60s /workspace/regression_test.go\n```\n\n### Within Repository Context\n```bash\ncd /workspace\ngo test -run TestRegression -v -timeout 60s ./regression_test.go\n```\n\n## Expected Test Behavior\n\n### Current State (Buggy Code)\nThe tests will likely:\n- ✓ Pass: Device registration (multiple devices can be added)\n- ✓ Pass: Device isolation (unique key handles, device separation)\n- ✗ Fail: Challenge generation would fail in actual login (but limited testing via public API)\n\n### Why Tests Don't Fully Demonstrate Bug\nThe public API doesn't expose the internal `mfaAuthChallenge()` method that generates login challenges for all devices.
